4 General Description:
5 This bill addresses economic development planning and programs within the Governor's Office of
Economic {Opportunity} Development.
7 Highlighted Provisions:
8 This bill:
9 ▸ defines terms and modifies definitions;
1 0 ▸ renames the Governor's Office of Economic Opportunity to the Governor's Office of
Economic Development;
1 0 ▸ modifies the duties of the executive director of the Governor's Office of Economic {Opportunity
} Development (executive director);
1 2 ▸ establishes the Economic Opportunity Coordinating Council (council);
1 3 ▸ describes the membership of the council;
1 4 ▸ describes the duties of the council;
1 5 ▸ requires the council to create a work group to provide oversight for the opportunity zone
application process in 2026;

1 7 ▸ establishes reporting requirements for the council;
1 8 ▸ beginning January 1, 2028, requires the executive director to provide an annual written report to
the Economic Development and Workforce Services Interim Committee;
2 0 ▸ modifies the requirements for the creation of an economic development zone; {and}
2 3 ▸ includes revisor instructions; and
2 1 ▸ makes technical and conforming changes.

207 9-9-104.6. Participation of state agencies in meetings with tribal leaders -- Contact
information.
209 (1) For at least three of the joint meetings described in Subsection 9-9-104.5(2)(a), the division shall
coordinate with representatives of tribal governments and the entities listed in Subsection (2) to
provide for the broadest participation possible in the joint meetings.
213 (2) The following may participate in all meetings described in Subsection (1):
214 (a) the chairs of the Native American Legislative Liaison Committee created in Section 36-22-1;
216 (b) the governor or the governor's designee;

53F-5-604; and

(a) The chief administrative officer of the agencies listed in Subsection (3)(b) shall:

256 Section 2. Section 9-9-112 is amended to read:
257 9-9-112. Bears Ears Visitor Center Advisory Committee.
259 (1) Utah extends an invitation to the Navajo Nation, the Ute Mountain Ute Tribe, the Hopi Nation, the
Zuni Tribe, and the Ute Indian Tribe of the Uintah Ouray to form an advisory committee for the
- 9 -

HB0475 compared with HB0475S01
purpose of exploring the feasibility, location, functions, and other important matters surrounding the
creation of a visitor center at Bears Ears.
263 (2) As used in this section:
264 (a) "Advisory committee" means the Bears Ears Visitor Center Advisory Committee created by this
section.
266 (b) "Bears Ears" means the Bears Ears National Monument.
267 (3)
(a) Subject to Subsection (3)(b), there is created the Bears Ears Visitor Center Advisory Committee
consisting of the following voting members:
269 (i) a representative of the Navajo Nation, appointed by the Navajo Nation;
270 (ii) a representative of the Ute Mountain Ute Tribe, appointed by the Ute Mountain Ute Tribe;
272 (iii) a representative of the Hopi Nation, appointed by the Hopi Nation;
273 (iv) a representative of the Zuni Tribe, appointed by the Zuni Tribe; and
274 (v) a representative of the Ute Indian Tribe of the Uintah Ouray, appointed by the Ute Indian Tribe
of the Uintah Ouray.
276 (b) The advisory committee is formed when all of the tribes described in Subsection (1) have
communicated to the other tribes and to the Division of Indian Affairs that the tribe has appointed a
member to the advisory committee.
279 (c)
(i) The president of the Senate and the speaker of the House of Representatives may each appoint to the
advisory committee one nonvoting individual.
281 (ii) If an individual appointed under Subsection (3)(c)(i) is a member of the Legislature, the member
serves as a member of the public and not in the member's legislative capacity.
284 (4) The advisory committee may select from the advisory committee members the chair or other
officers of the advisory committee.
286 (5)
(a) If a vacancy occurs in the membership of the advisory committee appointed under Subsection (3),
the member shall be replaced in the same manner in which the original appointment was made.
289 (b) A member appointed under Subsection (3) serves until the member's successor is appointed and
qualified.
291 (6)
- 10 -

HB0475 compared with HB0475S01
(a) A majority of the voting members of the advisory committee constitutes a quorum.
292 (b) The action of a majority of a quorum constitutes an action of the advisory committee.
293 (7) An advisory committee member may not receive compensation or benefits for the member's service
on the advisory committee, but may receive per diem and reimbursement for travel expenses
incurred as an advisory committee member at the rates established by the Division of Finance under:
297 (a) Sections 63A-3-106 and 63A-3-107; and
298 (b) rules made by the Division of Finance pursuant to Sections 63A-3-106 and 63A-3-107.
300 (8) The advisory committee may invite the United States Forest Service, the Bureau of Land
Management, the Division of State Parks, the Division of Outdoor Recreation, and the Utah Office
of Tourism within the Governor's Office of Economic [Opportunity] Development, to serve as
technical advisors to the advisory committee.
304 (9) The Division of Indian Affairs shall staff the advisory committee.
305 (10) The advisory committee shall study and make recommendations concerning:
306 (a) the need for a visitor center associated with Bears Ears;
307 (b) the feasibility of a visitor center associated with Bears Ears, including investigating:
308 (i) potential locations for the visitor center;
309 (ii) purposes for the visitor center; and
310 (iii) sources of funding to build and maintain the visitor center;
311 (c) whether a visitor center will increase visitorship to Bears Ears; and
312 (d) whether a visitor center at Bears Ears could function as a repository of traditional knowledge and
practices.
314 (11) The advisory committee may contract with one or more consultants to conduct work related to the
issues raised in Subsection (10) if the Legislature appropriates money expressly for the purpose of
the advisory committee contracting with a consultant.
317 (12) The advisory committee shall hold at least one public hearing to obtain public comment on the
creation of a Bears Ears visitor center.
319 (13) The advisory committee shall report the advisory committee's recommendations to one or more of
the following:
321 (a) the Economic Development and Workforce Services Interim Committee;
322 (b) the House Economic Development and Workforce Services Committee; or
323 (c) the Senate Economic Development and Workforce Services Committee.

324 Section 3. Section 10-21-203 is amended to read:
325 10-21-203. Station area plan requirements -- Contents -- Review and certification by
applicable metropolitan planning organization.
327 (1)
(a) Subject to the requirements of this section, a municipality that has a fixed guideway public transit
station located within the municipality's boundaries shall, for the station area:
330 (i) develop and adopt a station area plan; and
331 (ii) adopt any appropriate land use regulations to implement the station area plan.
332 (b) The requirements of Subsection (1)(a) shall be considered satisfied if:
333 (i)
(A) the municipality has already adopted plans or ordinances, approved land use applications, approved
agreements or financing, or investments have been made, before June 1, 2022, that substantially
promote each of the objectives in Subsection (6)(a) within the station area, and can demonstrate
that such plans, ordinances, approved land use applications, approved agreements or financing, or
investments are still relevant to making meaningful progress towards achieving such objectives; and
340 (B) the municipality adopts a resolution finding that the objectives of Subsection (6)(a) have been
substantially promoted; or
342 (ii)
(A) the municipality has determined that conditions exist that make satisfying a portion or all of the
requirements of Subsection (1)(a) for a station area impracticable, including conditions that relate
to existing development, entitlements, land ownership, land uses that make opportunities for new
development and long-term redevelopment infeasible, environmental limitations, market readiness,
development impediment conditions, or other similar conditions; and
349 (B) the municipality adopts a resolution describing the conditions that exist to make satisfying the
requirements of Subsection (1)(a) impracticable.
351 (c) To the extent that previous actions by a municipality do not satisfy the requirements of Subsection
(1)(a) for a station area, the municipality shall take the actions necessary to satisfy those
requirements.
354 (2)
(a) A municipality that has a new fixed guideway public transit station located within the municipality's
boundaries shall satisfy the requirements of Subsection (1)(a) for the station area surrounding the
- 12 -

HB0475 compared with HB0475S01
new fixed guideway public transit station before the new fixed guideway public transit station
begins transit services.
358 (b) Except as provided in Subsections (2)(c) and (d), a municipality that has an existing fixed guideway
public transit station located within the municipality's boundaries shall satisfy the requirements of
Subsection (1)(a) for the station area surrounding the existing fixed guideway public transit station
on or before December 31, 2025.
362 (c) If a municipality has more than four existing fixed guideway public transit stations located within
the municipality's boundaries, the municipality shall:
364 (i) on or before December 31, 2025, satisfy the requirements of Subsection (1)(a) for four or more
station areas located within the municipality; and
366 (ii) on or before December 31 of each year thereafter, satisfy the requirements of Subsection (1)(a) for
no less than two station areas located within the municipality until the municipality has satisfied the
requirements of Subsection (1)(a) for each station area located within the municipality.
370 (d)
(i) Subject to Subsection (2)(d)(ii):
371 (A) if a municipality receives a complete qualifying land use petition on or before July 1, 2022, the
municipality shall satisfy the requirements of Subsection (1)(a) for the station area in which the
development is proposed on or before July 1, 2023; and
375 (B) if a municipality receives a complete qualifying land use petition after July 1, 2022, the
municipality shall satisfy the requirements of Subsection (1)(a) for the station area in which
the development is proposed within a 12-month period beginning on the first day of the month
immediately following the month in which the qualifying land use petition is submitted to the
municipality, and shall notify the applicable metropolitan planning organization of the receipt of
the qualified land use petition within 45 days of the date of receipt.
383 (ii)
(A) A municipality is not required to satisfy the requirements of Subsection (1)(a) for more than two
station areas under Subsection (2)(d)(i) within any 12-month period.
386 (B) If a municipality receives more than two complete qualifying land use petitions on or before July
1, 2022, the municipality shall select two station areas for which the municipality will satisfy the
requirements of Subsection (1)(a) in accordance with Subsection (2)(d)(i)(A).

(iii) A municipality shall process on a first priority basis a land use application, including an application
for a building permit, if:
392 (A) the land use application is for a residential use within a station area for which the municipality has
not satisfied the requirements of Subsection (1)(a); and
394 (B) the municipality would be required to change a zoning designation for the land use application to be
approved.
396 (e) Notwithstanding Subsections (2)(a) through (d), the time period for satisfying the requirements of
Subsection (1)(a) for a station area may be extended once for a period of 12 months if:
399 (i) the municipality demonstrates to the applicable metropolitan planning organization that conditions
exist that make satisfying the requirements of Subsection (1)(a) within the required time period
infeasible, despite the municipality's good faith efforts; and
403 (ii) the applicable metropolitan planning organization certifies to the municipality in writing that the
municipality satisfied the demonstration in Subsection (2)(e)(i).
405 (3)
(a) Except as provided in Subsection (3)(b), if a station area is included within the boundaries of more
than one municipality, each municipality with jurisdiction over the station area shall satisfy the
requirements of Subsection (1)(a) for the portion of the station area over which the municipality has
jurisdiction.
409 (b) Two or more municipalities with jurisdiction over a station area may coordinate to develop a shared
station area plan for the entire station area.
411 (4) A municipality that has more than one fixed guideway public transit station located within the
municipality may, through an integrated process, develop station area plans for multiple station
areas if the station areas are within close proximity of each other.
414 (5)
(a) A municipality that is required to develop and adopt a station area plan under this section may
request technical assistance from the applicable metropolitan planning organization.
417 (b) An applicable metropolitan planning organization that receives funds from the Governor's Office
of Economic [Opportunity] Development under Section 63N-3-113 shall, when utilizing the funds,
give priority consideration to requests for technical assistance for station area plans required under
Subsection (2)(d).
421 (6)
- 14 -

HB0475 compared with HB0475S01
(a) A station area plan shall promote the following objectives within the station area:
422 (i) increasing the availability and affordability of housing, including moderate income housing;
424 (ii) promoting sustainable environmental conditions;
425 (iii) enhancing access to opportunities; and
426 (iv) increasing transportation choices and connections.

implementing the following actions:

general plan;
431 (B) providing for densities necessary to facilitate the development of moderate income housing;
433 (C) providing for affordable costs of living in connection with housing, transportation, and parking;
or
435 (D) any other similar action that promotes the objective described in Subsection (6)(a)(i).
437 (ii) To promote the objective described in Subsection (6)(a)(ii), a municipality may consider
implementing the following actions:
439 (A) conserving water resources through efficient land use;
440 (B) improving air quality by reducing fuel consumption and motor vehicle trips;
441 (C) establishing parks, open spaces, and recreational opportunities; or

1021 Section 16. Section 17C-1-1001 is amended to read:
1022 17C-1-1001. Definitions.
As used in this part:
1024 (1)
(a) "Agency-wide project development" means activity within the agency's boundaries that, as
determined by the board, encourages, promotes, or provides development or redevelopment for the
purpose of achieving the results described in an implementation plan, including affordable housing.
1028
- 32 -

HB0475 compared with HB0475S01
(b) "Agency-wide project development" does not include project area development under a project area
plan.
1030 (2) "Certified tax rate" means the same as that term is defined in Section 59-2-924.
1031 (3) "Cooperative development project" means project area development with impacts that extend
beyond an agency's geographic boundaries to the benefit of two or more communities.
1034 (4) "Economic development project" means project area development for the purpose of:
1035 (a) creating, developing, attracting, and retaining business;
1036 (b) creating or preserving jobs;
1037 (c) stimulating business and economic activity; or
1038 (d) providing a local incentive as required by the Governor's Office of Economic
[Opportunity] Development under Title 63N, Economic Opportunity Act.
1040 (5) "Eligible taxing entity" means a taxing entity that:
1041 (a) is a municipality, a county, or a school district; and
1042 (b) contains an agency partially or completely within the taxing entity's geographic boundaries.
1044 (6) "Final tax rate" means:
1045 (a) the certified rate; or
1046 (b) if the agency adopts a rate that is different than the certified rate, the rate the agency adopts in
accordance with the provisions of Title 59, Chapter 2, Part 9, Levies.
1048 (7) "Implementation plan" means a plan adopted in accordance with Section 17C-1-1004 that:
1050 (a) describes how the agency uses property tax revenue; and
1051 (b) guides and controls agency-wide project development.
1052 (8) "Project area incremental revenue" means the amount of revenue generated by the incremental value
that a taxing entity receives after a project area funds collection period ends.
1055 (9) "Property tax revenue" means the amount of revenue generated by an agency from the property
within the agency using the current taxable value of the property and the agency's final tax rate.

1113 35A-1-104.5. Other department duties -- Strategic plan for health system reform --
Reporting suspected misuse of a social security number.
1115 (1) The department shall work with the Department of Health and Human Services, the Insurance
Department, the Governor's Office of Economic [Opportunity] Development, and the Legislature to
develop the health system reform.
1118 (2) In the process of determining an individual's eligibility for a public benefit or service under this title
or under federal law, if the department determines that a valid social security number is being used
by an unauthorized individual, the department shall:
1121 (a) inform the individual who the department determines to be the likely actual owner of the social
security number or, if the likely actual owner is a minor, the minor's parent or guardian, of the
suspected misuse; and
1124 (b) subject to federal law, provide information of the suspected misuse to an appropriate law
enforcement agency responsible for investigating identity fraud.
1126 (3) If the department learns or determines that providing information under Subsection (2)(b) is
prohibited by federal law, the department shall notify the Legislative Management Committee.

3268 (b) may not exceed the lesser of:

obtaining access; and

4515 Section 64. Section 63G-4-102 is amended to read:
4516 63G-4-102. Scope and applicability of chapter.
4517 (1) Except as set forth in Subsection (2), and except as otherwise provided by a statute superseding
provisions of this chapter by explicit reference to this chapter, the provisions of this chapter apply to
every agency of the state and govern:
4520 (a) state agency action that determines the legal rights, duties, privileges, immunities, or other legal
interests of an identifiable person, including agency action to grant, deny, revoke, suspend, modify,
annul, withdraw, or amend an authority, right, or license; and
4524 (b) judicial review of the action.
4525 (2) This chapter does not govern:
4526 (a) the procedure for making agency rules, or judicial review of the procedure or rules;
4527 (b) the issuance of a notice of a deficiency in the payment of a tax, the decision to waive a penalty
or interest on taxes, the imposition of and penalty or interest on taxes, or the issuance of a tax
assessment, except that this chapter governs an agency action commenced by a taxpayer or by
another person authorized by law to contest the validity or correctness of the action;
4532 (c) state agency action relating to extradition, to the granting of a pardon or parole, a commutation or

4646 63G-21-102. Definitions.

4648 (1) "Designated agency" means:

4916 63M-5-306. Financial impact statement -- Alleviation plan -- Filing required -- Contents --
Payments credited against tax -- Provisions neither exclusive nor mandatory.
4919 (1)
(a) A developer desiring to prepay ad valorem property taxes under Section 63M-5-201 shall first
prepare and file with the Governor's Office of Economic [Opportunity] Development and all units of
local government likely to be affected with a significant financial impact due to a natural resource or
industrial facility a financial impact statement together with a plan for alleviating these impacts.
4924 (b) The impact statement and the alleviation plan shall be prepared in cooperation with and after
consultation with the Governor's Office of Economic [Opportunity] Development and the affected
units of local government.
4927 (c) The financial impact statement shall assess the projected financial impact on state agencies and units
of local government, including the impact on transportation systems, culinary water systems, waste
treatment facilities, public safety, schools, public health, housing, planning and zoning, and general
government administration.
4931 (d) The alleviation plan shall set out proposals for alleviating the impact and may include payments to
local units of government or direct expenditures by the developer to alleviate the impact.
4934 (e) The impact statement and the alleviation plan may be amended by the developer in cooperation with
and after consultation with the Governor's Office of Economic Opportunity and those units of local
government affected by the amendment.
4937 (2) At least 90 days prior to commencement of construction of an industrial facility or natural resources
facility by a major developer, an impact statement and alleviation plan as described in Subsection
(1) shall be filed by the major developer regardless of whether [or not ]the major developer desires
to prepay ad valorem property taxes.
4941 (3)
(a) Upon the filing of the financial impact statement and alleviation plan, a developer may apply to the
governing body of the affected unit of local government for authorization to prepay a portion of the
anticipated ad valorem property taxes to be expended consistent with the alleviation plan.
4945 (b) This authorization may provide that only a portion of the amounts so prepaid can be applied against
the ad valorem property taxes due in any given year.
4947 (c) In addition to payments directly to the affected unit of local government, an affected unit of local
government may authorize a tax credit on anticipated ad valorem property taxes for expenditures
- 149 -

HB0475 compared with HB0475S01
made by the developer to other persons so long as the expenditure is consistent with the alleviation
plan.
4951 (4)
(a) This chapter is designed to provide an additional mechanism for the alleviation of impacts on units
of local government and is not intended to discourage the use of other mechanisms as may be
available.
4954 (b) Nothing in this chapter requires a developer to prepay ad valorem property taxes or to make any
other expenditure not otherwise required by law.

5094 Section 74. Section 63N-1a-103 is amended to read:
5095 63N-1a-103. Purpose.
5096 (1) The purpose of the Economic Opportunity Act and the entities established in the act is to catalyze
strategic economic development opportunities for all residents of the state with a vision of creating
economically thriving communities, businesses, and families throughout the state.
5100 (2) The purpose is realized through targeted efforts that demonstrably improve quality of life, measured
by the extent to which the efforts accomplish the following strategic goals:
5102 (a) catalyzing targeted industry growth;
5103 (b) supporting economically thriving communities;
5104 (c) empowering students and workers with market-relevant skills;
5105 (d) stimulating economic growth in rural and multicultural communities through household level
efforts; and
5107 (e) securing healthy and resilient ecosystems for current and future generations.
5108 Section 75. Section 63N-1a-301 is amended to read:
5109 63N-1a-301. Creation of office -- Responsibilities.
5110 (1) There is created the Governor's Office of Economic [Opportunity] Development.
5111 (2) The office is:
5112 (a) responsible for creating and implementing the statewide economic development strategy that:
5114 (i) unifies and coordinates economic development efforts in the state;
5115 (ii) includes key performance indicators for long-term progress toward the state strategic goals;
5117 (iii) establishes reporting and accountability processes for the key performance indicators; and
5119 (iv) ensures the success of statewide economic development; and
5120 (b) the industrial and business promotion authority of the state.
- 154 -

HB0475 compared with HB0475S01
5121 (3) The office shall:
5122 (a) consistent with the statewide economic development strategy, coordinate and align into a single
effort the activities of the economic opportunity agencies in the field of economic development;
5125 (b) provide support and direction to economic opportunity agencies in establishing goals, metrics, and
activities that align with the statewide economic development strategy;
5128 (c) administer and coordinate state and federal economic development grant programs;
5129 (d) promote and encourage the economic, commercial, financial, industrial, agricultural, and civic
welfare of the state;
5131 (e) develop the statewide economic development strategy consistent with the state water policy
described in Section 73-1-21, including the state's commitment to appropriate:
5133 (i) conservation;
5134 (ii) efficient and optimal use of water resources;
5135 (iii) infrastructure development and improvement;
5136 (iv) optimal agricultural use;
5137 (v) water quality;
5138 (vi) reasonable access to recreational activities;
5139 (vii) effective wastewater treatment; and
5140 (viii) protecting and restoring health ecosystems;
5141 (f) at least once every five years, identify which industry or groups of industries shall be targeted for
economic development in the state;
5143 (g) promote and encourage the employment of workers in the state and the purchase of goods and
services produced in the state by local businesses;
5145 (h) act to create, develop, attract, and retain business, industry, and commerce in the state:
5147 (i) in accordance with the statewide economic development strategy; and
5148 (ii) subject to the restrictions in Section 11-41-103;
5149 (i) act to enhance the state's economy;
5150 (j) analyze the state's projected long-term population and economic growth and plan for the anticipated
impacts of the projected growth in a manner that improves quality of life and is consistent with the
statewide economic development strategy and state strategic goals;

308 (1) The office may create an economic development zone in the state if the following requirements are

incentives within the area in accordance with the local government entity's approved incentive
policy.

327 (ii) workforce development; and

5456 Section 84. Section 63N-2-104.2 is amended to read:
5457 63N-2-104.2. Written agreement -- Contents -- Grounds for amendment or termination.
5459 (1) If the office determines that a business entity is eligible for a tax credit under Section 63N-2-104.1,
the office may enter into a written agreement with the business entity that:
5461 (a) establishes performance benchmarks for the business entity to claim a tax credit, including any
minimum wage requirements;
5463
- 164 -

HB0475 compared with HB0475S01
(b) specifies the maximum amount of tax credit that the business entity may be authorized for a
taxable year and over the life of the new commercial project, subject to the limitations in Section
63N-2-104.3;
5466 (c) establishes the length of time the business entity may claim a tax credit;
5467 (d) requires the business entity to retain records supporting a claim for a tax credit for at least four years
after the business entity claims the tax credit;
5469 (e) requires the business entity to submit to audits for verification of any tax credit claimed; and
5471 (f) requires the business entity, in order to claim a tax credit, to meet the requirements of Section
63N-2-105.
5473 (2) In establishing the terms of a written agreement, including the duration and amount of tax credit that
the business entity may be authorized to receive, the office shall:
5475 (a) authorize the tax credit in a manner that provides the most effective incentive for the new
commercial project;
5477 (b) consider the following factors:
5478 (i) whether the new commercial project provides vital or specialized support to supply chains;
5480 (ii) whether the new commercial project provides an innovative product, technology, or service;
5482 (iii) the number and wages of new incremental jobs associated with the new commercial project;
5484 (iv) the amount of financial support provided by local government entities for the new commercial
project;
5486 (v) the amount of capital expenditures associated with the new commercial project;
5487 (vi) whether the new commercial project returns jobs transferred overseas;
5488 (vii) the rate of unemployment in the county in which the new commercial project is located;
5490 (viii) whether the new commercial project creates a remote work opportunity;
5491 (ix) whether the new commercial project is located in a development zone created by a local
government entity as described in Subsection 63N-2-104(2);
5493 (x) whether the business entity commits to hiring Utah workers for the new commercial project;
5495 (xi) whether the business entity adopts a corporate citizenry plan or supports initiatives in the state that
advance education, gender equality, diversity and inclusion, work-life balance, environmental or
social good, or other similar causes;
5498 (xii) whether the business entity's headquarters are located within the state;
5499
- 165 -

HB0475 compared with HB0475S01
(xiii) the likelihood of other business entities relocating to another state as a result of the new
commercial project;
5501 (xiv) the necessity of the tax credit for the business entity's expansion in the state or relocation from
another state;
5503 (xv) whether the proposed new commercial project might reasonably be expected to occur in the
foreseeable future without the tax credit; and
5505 (xvi) the location and impact of the new commercial project on existing and planned transportation
facilities, existing and planned housing, including affordable housing, and public infrastructure; and
5508 (c) consult with the [GOEO] GOED board.

and
5514 (b) establish by rule made in accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking
Act, a process by which the office closely approximates the amount of taxes the business entity paid
under Title 59, Chapter 12, Sales and Use Tax Act, for a capital project.
5518 (4) If the office identifies any of the following events after entering into a written agreement with a
business entity, the office and the business entity shall amend, or the office may terminate, the
written agreement:
5521 (a) a change in the business entity's organization resulting from a merger with or acquisition of another
entity located in the state;
5523 (b) a material increase in the business entity's retail operations that results in new state revenue not
subject to the incentive; or

5526 (i) is outside the scope of the written agreement or outside the boundaries of a development zone; and
5528 (ii) results in new state revenue not subject to the incentive.

5681 63N-3-112. Talent development grants.

overseas.

6374 (iii) any existing or planned partnerships between the entity and another individual or entity to
implement the proposal.

6379 (ii) the extent to which any additional funding sources or existing or planned partnerships will benefit

6407 Section 100. Section 63N-3-1602 is amended to read:
6408 63N-3-1602. Applicability, requirements, and limitations on a first home investment zone.
6410 (1) A first home investment zone created in accordance with this part shall promote the following
objectives:
6412 (a) encouraging efficient development and opportunities for home ownership by providing a variety of
housing options, including affordable housing and for sale, owner-occupied housing;
6415 (b) improving availability of housing options;
6416 (c) overcoming development impediments and market conditions that render a development cost
prohibitive absent the proposal and incentives;
6418 (d) conserving water resources through efficient land use;
6419 (e) improving air quality by reducing fuel consumption and motor vehicle trips;
- 193 -

HB0475 compared with HB0475S01
6420 (f) encouraging transformative mixed-use development;
6421 (g) strategic land use and municipal planning in major transit investment corridors as described in
Subsection 10-20-404(2);
6423 (h) increasing access to employment and educational opportunities;
6424 (i) increasing access to child care; and
6425 (j) improving efficiencies in parking and transportation, including walkability of communities, street
and path interconnectivity within the proposed development and connections to surrounding
communities, and access to roadways, public transportation, and active transportation.
6429 (2) In order to accomplish the objectives described in Subsection (1), a municipality or county that
initiates the process to create a first home investment zone as described in this part shall ensure that
the proposal for a first home investment zone includes:
6432 (a) subject to Subsection (3), a minimum of 30 housing units per acre:
6433 (i) in at least 51% of the developable area within the first home investment zone; and
6434 (ii) of which 50% must be owner occupied;
6435 (b) a mixed use development;
6436 (c) a requirement that at least 25% of homes within the first home investment zone remain owner
occupied for at least 25 years from the date of original purchase;
6438 (d) for homes inside the first home investment zone, a requirement that at least 12% of the owner
occupied homes and 12% of the homes that are not owner occupied are affordable housing;
6441 (e) a requirement that at least 20% of the extraterritorial homes are affordable housing; and
6443 (f) except for extraterritorial homes, the number of homes that result from multiplying the number of
housing units described in Subsection (2)(a) by the developable area described in Subsection (2)(a)
(i) may be intermingled with other mixed uses within the first home investment zone.
6447 (3)
(a) Subject to Subsection (3)(b), to satisfy the requirements described in Subsection (2)(a), a first home
investment zone may include an extraterritorial home to count toward the required density and
owner-occupancy of the first home investment zone by:
6451 (i) adding the total number of extraterritorial homes related to the first home investment zone to the
total number of homes within the first home investment zone; and
6454 (ii) dividing the sum described in Subsection (3)(a)(i) by a number equal to 51% of the total number
of developable acres within the first home investment zone.
- 194 -

HB0475 compared with HB0475S01
6456 (b) Extraterritorial homes may account for no more than half of the total homes to calculate density
within a first home investment zone.
6458 (4)
(a) If a municipality proposes a first home investment zone, the proposal shall comply with the
limitations described in this Subsection (4).
6460 (b) A first home investment zone may not be less than 10 acres and no more than 100 acres of
developable area in size.
6462 (c)
(i) Except as provided in Subsection (4)(c)(ii), a first home investment zone is required to be one
contiguous area.
6464 (ii) While considering a first home investment zone proposal as described in Section 63N-3-1605, the
housing and transit reinvestment zone committee may consider and approve a first home investment
zone that is not one contiguous area if:
6467 (A) the municipality provides evidence in the proposal showing that the deviation from the contiguity
requirement will enhance the ability of the first home investment zone to achieve the objectives
described in Subsection (1); and
6470 (B) the housing and transit reinvestment zone committee determines that the deviation is reasonable and
circumstances justify deviation from the contiguity requirement.
6473 (iii) The first home investment zone area contiguity is not affected by roads or other rights-of-way.

6482 (iii) Subject to Subsection (4)(d)(iv), a municipality shall ensure that the required affordable housing
units are included proportionally in each phase of the first home investment zone development.
6485 (iv) A municipality may allow a first home investment zone to be phased and developed in a manner to
provide more of the required affordable housing units in early phases of development.
6488
- 195 -

HB0475 compared with HB0475S01
(e) If a municipality proposes a first home investment zone, commencement of the collection of tax
increment, for all or a portion of the first home investment zone, is triggered by providing notice as
described in Subsection (5).
6491 (f) A municipality may restrict homes within a first home investment zone and related extraterritorial
homes from being used as a short-term rental.
6493 (g) A municipality shall ensure that affordable housing within a first home investment zone and related
extraterritorial homes that are reserved as affordable housing are spread throughout the overall

6496 (h) A municipality shall ensure that at least 80% of extraterritorial homes included in a first home

(a) After receiving the proposal as described in Subsection (1)(c), the Governor's Office of Economic

6788 63N-16-102. Definitions.
As used in this chapter:

types of authorization, which the office determines would otherwise regulate a sandbox participant.
6796 (3) "Applicant" means a person that applies to participate in the regulatory sandbox.
6797 (4) "Blockchain technology" means the use of a digital database containing records of financial
transactions, which can be simultaneously used and shared within a decentralized, publicly
accessible network and can record transactions between two parties in a verifiable and permanent
way.
6801 (5) "Consumer" means a person that purchases or otherwise enters into a transaction or agreement to
receive an offering pursuant to a demonstration by a sandbox participant.
6803 (6) "Demonstrate" or "demonstration" means to temporarily provide an offering in accordance with the
provisions of the regulatory sandbox program described in this chapter.
6806 (7) "Director" means the director of the Utah Office of Regulatory Relief created in Section
63N-16-103.
6808 (8) "Executive director" means the executive director of the Governor's Office of Economic
[Opportunity] Development.
6810 (9) "Financial product or service" means:
6811 (a) a financial product or financial service that requires state licensure or registration; or
6812 (b) a financial product, financial service, or banking business that includes a business model,
delivery mechanism, offering of deposit accounts, or element that may require a license or other
authorization to act as a financial institution, enterprise, or other entity that is regulated by Title 7,
Financial Institutions Act, or other related provisions.
6817 (10) "Health, safety, and financial well-being" includes protecting against physical injury, property
damage, or financial harm.
- 205 -

HB0475 compared with HB0475S01
6819 (11) "Innovation" means the use or incorporation of a new or existing idea, a new or emerging
technology, or a new use of existing technology, including blockchain technology, to address a
problem, provide a benefit, or otherwise offer a product, production method, or service.
6823 (12) "Insurance product or service" means an insurance product or insurance service that requires state
licensure, registration, or other authorization as regulated by Title 31A, Insurance Code, including
an insurance product or insurance service that includes a business model, delivery mechanism, or
element that requires a license, registration, or other authorization to do an insurance business, act
as an insurance producer or consultant, or engage in insurance adjusting as regulated by Title 31A,
Insurance Code.
6829 (13)

or an insurance product or service, that includes an innovation.

Chapter 1, Utah Uniform Securities Act.

6846 (18) "Sandbox participant" means a person whose application to participate in the regulatory sandbox is
approved in accordance with the provisions of this chapter.
6848 (19) "Service" means any commercial activity, duty, or labor performed for another person.

7686 Section 120. Section 79-7-203 is amended to read:
7687 79-7-203. Powers and duties of division.
7688 (1) As used in this section, "real property" includes land under water, upland, and all other property
commonly or legally defined as real property.
7690 (2) The Division of Wildlife Resources shall retain the power and jurisdiction conferred upon the
Division of Wildlife Resources by law on property controlled by the division with reference to fish
and game.
- 232 -

HB0475 compared with HB0475S01
7693 (3) For purposes of property controlled by the division, the division shall permit multiple uses of the
property for purposes such as grazing, fishing, hunting, camping, mining, and the development and
use of water and other natural resources.
7696 (4)
(a) The division may acquire real and personal property in the name of the state by legal and proper
means, including purchase, gift, devise, eminent domain, lease, exchange, or otherwise, subject to
the approval of the executive director and the governor.
7700 (b) In acquiring real or personal property, the credit of the state may not be pledged without the consent
of the Legislature.
7702 (5)
(a) Before acquiring any real property, the division shall notify the county legislative body of the county
where the property is situated of the division's intention to acquire the property.
7705 (b) If the county legislative body requests a hearing within 10 days of receipt of the notice, the division
shall hold a public hearing in the county concerning the matter.
7707 (6) Acceptance of gifts or devises of land or other property is at the discretion of the division, subject to
the approval of the executive director and the governor.
7709 (7) The division shall acquire property by eminent domain in the manner authorized by Title 78B,
Chapter 6, Part 5, Eminent Domain.
7711 (8)
(a) The division may make charges for special services and use of facilities, the income from which is
available for recreation purposes.
7713 (b) The division may conduct and operate those services necessary for the comfort and convenience of
the public.
7715 (9)
(a) The division may lease or rent concessions of lawful kinds and nature on property to persons,
partnerships, and corporations for a valuable consideration after notifying the commission.
7718 (b) The division shall comply with Title 63G, Chapter 6a, Utah Procurement Code, in selecting
concessionaires.
7720 (10) The division shall proceed without delay to negotiate with the federal government concerning the
Weber Basin and other recreation and reclamation projects.

7763 Section 122. Revisor instructions.
The Legislature intends that, on May 6, 2026, all references to the term "GOEO" change
to "GOED" and all references to the term "Governor's Office of Economic Opportunity"
change to "Governor's Office of Economic Development" in any new language added to the
Utah Code by legislation that passes in the 2026 General Session and becomes law.
